1895-09-12 00:00:00 Scene 0 --- Participants: ['Della Plumstone', 'Lennon Figtree']
    Event statement
  • Della Plumstone -- premise: The first rays of dawn painted the sky above Fruitville in hues of orange and gold, casting a warm glow over the bustling market. Stalls overflowed with vibrant fruits, their aromas mingling in the crisp morning air. Della Plumstone is trying to buy some fruit from Lennon Figtree. They are negotiating a price. Della Plumstone can sell the fruit for 6 coins back in her home town.
    Lennon Figtree -- premise: The first rays of dawn painted the sky above Fruitville in hues of orange and gold, casting a warm glow over the bustling market. Stalls overflowed with vibrant fruits, their aromas mingling in the crisp morning air. Lennon Figtree is trying to sell some fruit. He is negotiating a price with Della Plumstone. It costs Lennon Figtree 1 coin to buy the fruit from the farm.

1895-09-12 00:00:00 Lennon Figtree -- Lennon Figtree -- "Now Della, you know these peaches are the finest in Fruitville. I can't just give them away.

          [28 Oct 1872 00:00:00]
          [28 Oct 1875 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 6 years old, she witnessed a travelling merchant arrive in her bustling marketplace. She was mesmerized by the colorful display of exotic fruits, their scents intoxicating her senses. Della vowed then and there to one day own a cart just like his, filled with treasures from faraway lands.
          [28 Oct 1879 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 9 years old, she overheard two women gossiping about her mother. They whispered about her sadness, her withdrawn nature, and how she kept to herself. Della, hiding behind a stack of crates, felt a pang of empathy for her mother, understanding for the first time the weight of loneliness.
          [28 Oct 1882 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 13 years old, she helped her father barter for a crate of bruised peaches. The vendor, a gruff man with a booming laugh, tried to cheat them, but Della, armed with her quick wit and a charming smile, negotiated a fair price. It was then she realized the power of words, the art of persuasion, and the thrill of a successful trade.
          [28 Oct 1885 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 16 years old, she experienced her first heartbreak. A young man, the son of a baker, had shown her kindness and shared his dreams of travelling the world. But when he left town, he never wrote, leaving Della with a hollow ache in her chest and a fear of letting anyone in again.
          [28 Oct 1887 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 19 years old, she convinced her father to let her take over the family fruit stall. She poured her heart into it, selecting the ripest fruits, arranging them artfully, and greeting customers with a warm smile. It was a small victory, a taste of independence and a step towards her dream of travelling the world.
          [28 Oct 1889 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 21 years old, she finally saved enough money to buy her own cart. It was a rickety old thing, but to Della, it was a symbol of freedom and possibility. With a heart full of hope and a touch of trepidation, she set off on her journey, leaving behind the familiar streets of her childhood.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

      Chain
    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

      Conversation history: Here is the conversation from the beginning:
      Lennon Figtree -- "Now Della, you know these peaches are the finest in Fruitville. I can't just give them away.
      Della Plumstone -- "Finest in Fruitville, maybe, but I've tasted peaches just as sweet back home for half the price. I'm willing to give you 4 coins a basket, and that's my final offer.
      Cedric Meadowbrook -- "Della, you know these peaches are top quality. They're worth every coin I'm asking. How about we split the difference? 4.

      Cedric Meadowbrook -- "Lennon, my friend, these peaches are ripe and juicy. A steal at 4 coins a basket.
      Lennon Figtree -- "Cedric, you know these peaches are worth more than that. I can get them for 3 coins a basket from young Thomas down the way.

Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.
